Standard for Hygiene Facilities in Primary Schools in Various Counties of Jiangsu

The standards for school hygiene facilities in primary schools in various counties of Jiangsu Province (drafted by Chen Bangxian) have been approved by the Provincial Health Education Committee. The original text is as follows:

Chapter One: Basic Principles of School Hygiene (1) School hygiene work should be the responsibility of teachers and staff. (2) When necessary, school hygiene work should be assisted by doctors, nurses, and oral hygienists. (3) Each school should have a hygiene room with a minimum level of hygiene equipment. (4) School hygiene work should focus on health education, with equal emphasis on behavior and knowledge. (5) School hygiene work should, in principle, make full use of children's activities. (6) The implementation of school hygiene must pay attention to the hygiene of the school environment. (7) The implementation of school hygiene must be linked to the students' families. (8) School hygiene personnel should lead by example. (9) Implementation of health checks must pay attention to the correction of shortcomings. (10) Prevention is more important than treatment.

Chapter Two: School Hygiene Administration

Each primary school should establish a school hygiene committee, composed of the principal, directors of teaching and academic affairs, teachers of all grades, and school doctors and nurses, to handle all school hygiene matters.

Chapter Three: School Health Education

Section One: Objectives of School Health Education (1) To cultivate children's hygienic habits to improve their physical and mental health. (2) To develop children's knowledge and skills in hygiene so that they can protect the health of individuals and the public. (3) To cultivate children's interest and confidence in hygiene, so that they can promote the improvement of life and the environment in the family, school, and society through personal efforts.

Section Two: School Health Teaching (1) Teaching materials: Teaching materials in the environment: A. Within the school: Various hygiene facilities and implementation within the school. B. Outside the school: Hygiene and medical institutions, hygiene facilities in the social environment, hygiene campaigns, etc. 2. Printed materials: A. Textbooks. B. Supplementary reading materials. 3. Integrated teaching materials: Teaching materials related to hygiene in other subjects, such as social studies and natural sciences. (2) Teaching methods: The principle is to make full use of integrated teaching methods and project-based teaching methods. (3) Reference books: Children's hygiene reference books: 1. Hygiene knowledge. 2. Medical common sense. 3. Medical and hygiene anecdotes. 4. Others.

Section Three: School Health Moral Education: Items of school health moral education: 1. Hygiene habit training. 2. Public hygiene lectures. 3. Morning meetings and literary society hygiene talks. 4. Dispersed lectures. 5. Personal talks. 6. Hygiene team training, including first aid training, trachoma training, and other training. 7. Others.

Chapter Four: Health Examination

Section One: Purpose of Health Examination: 1. To examine the development and health status of children. 2. To detect physical defects and early diseases in children for correction and treatment. 3. To cultivate children's awareness of the importance of their physical and mental health. 4. To promote parents' attention to children's health. 5. To cultivate children and their parents' concept of disease prevention.

Section Two: Procedure of Health Examination: 1. Height and weight. 2. Vision and hearing. 3. Ears. 4. Eyes. 5. Teeth. 6. Tonsils. 7. Nutrition. 8. Skin. 9. Heart and lungs. 10. Others.

Section Three: Health Examination Personnel: Teachers and staff are responsible for the examination, and doctors, nurses, or hygiene instructors from local health agencies may be invited to assist.

Section Four: Correction of Defects: If there are defects in the health examination, they can be corrected by local hospitals or doctors. The above examinations, such as in rural areas where it is difficult to find doctors and nurses, can be performed with a reduced number of items or simplified procedures.

Chapter Five: School Environmental Hygiene

(A) Conditions around the school building: (1) Quiet: such as not being near bustling markets, machine shops, or train stations. (2) No odors: such as from restaurants or manure yards. (3) No dangers: such as from gunpowder depots. (4) Convenient transportation, but without dust. (B) Classrooms: (1) Floor: Wooden or brick floors are acceptable, but solid, stable, and dust-free floors are preferred. (2) Wall color: Light green or light gray is suitable; white is suitable if the light is insufficient. (3) Windows and lighting: Light should come from the left. The area of paper windows should be one-third of the floor area of the entire classroom. The area of glass windows should be one-fifth of the floor area of the entire classroom. (4) Ventilation: Attention must be paid to air circulation. (5) Blackboard: Avoid glare and excessive roughness. The lower edge of the blackboard should be on a parallel line with the students' eyes. (6) Desks and chairs: The height of the chair should be equal to two-sevenths of the height. The height of the desk should be equal to three-sevenths of the height. There should be a negative distance of 5 cm between the desk and the chair. The distance from the edge of the chair to the back of the chair should be 25 cm to 36 cm. (7) Area: Each student should occupy at least two square meters. (8) Cleanliness: Pay attention to general cleanliness.

(C) Hygiene room: 1. Cleaning tools. 2. Medicines. 3. Record forms. (D) Teacher's office: 1. The volume should be sufficient. 2. Air circulation and sufficient light are required. 3. Special attention should be paid to tidiness and cleanliness.

(E) Sports field: 1. Each student should occupy at least 50 square feet of area. 2. The ground should be flat, without stones, and dust-free. 3. Equipment should be complete.

(F) Toilet:

(1) The number of toilet pits is listed in the table on the left. 2. There should be ten urinals for every 100 people. 3. There should be fly-proof and hand-washing facilities. 4. Attention should be paid to cleanliness.

(G) Disposal of garbage cans and incinerators: 1. Garbage cans should have lids. 2. Special attention should be paid to the removal of garbage cans and incinerators. Other improvements to the school environment, such as drinking water inspection and disinfection, are also within the scope of school environmental hygiene.

Chapter Six: Prevention and Handling of Infectious Diseases

(1) Report to the local health agency. (2) Notify parents to implement isolation. (3) Refuse entry to school. (4) Home visits. (5) Strict disinfection. (6) Vaccination: A. Vaccination (once per semester). B. Injecting vaccines or sera for cholera, typhoid, meningitis, and diphtheria.

Chapter Seven: Hygiene Activities

(1) Hygiene competition: 1. Cleanliness competition. 2. Hygiene book competition. 3. Hygiene speech competition. 4. Hygiene literary competition. 5. Other hygiene work competitions. (2) Hygiene publicity: 1. Drafting and making slogans and leaflets. 2. Parades and lectures. 3. Posting slogans. 4. Distributing leaflets. (3) Hygiene exhibition.

(4) Hygiene performance: 1. Singing and game performances. 2. Drama.

(5) Organize a hygiene team. 6. Other hygiene activities.

Key Points for Examining the Performance of Vocational Schools: Four Orders Issued by the Ministry of Education to Various Provinces and Cities

The Ministry of Education issued an order to the Education Bureaus of various provinces and cities on the 5th, stating that after repeatedly dispatching personnel to inspect the operation of vocational schools in various places, the Ministry found that the competent educational administrative authorities in various provinces and cities do not have a consistent and specific standard for evaluating the performance of schools, which can be used for reference. The Ministry has now formulated four key points to which attention should be paid when examining the performance of vocational schools, which are attached to the order. Please comply with them immediately and forward them to your subordinates for compliance. This is the order.

Key Points for Examining the Performance of Vocational Schools

(1) The educational administrative authorities of provinces and cities shall examine the performance of vocational schools in accordance with the provisions of these key points. (2) The key points of examination are divided into the following two types: A. Administrative facilities: 1. Whether the qualifications and experience of the principal and vocational subject teachers meet the regulations. 2. Whether the fees collected exceed the regulations and the amount by which they exceed. 3. Expenditure of funds and the percentage of equipment fees. 4. Whether the entire school is clean and suitable for use. Whether attention is paid to the hygiene of workshops and farms. 5. Whether the capacity of the practice site or the area of the farm and forest is sufficient for practical training in proportion to the number of students. 6. How is the condition of the newly added equipment? Whether the number of reference books, experimental instruments, and medicines for vocational subjects is sufficient for application in proportion to the number of students. 7. Whether the school has set up an advisory committee and how it is working. Whether there is close contact with the vocational industry. 8. The entrance examination scores of new students, and the percentage of those admitted with equivalent qualifications and their scores. 9. The ratio of the number of graduates in each class to the number of new students at the time of enrollment. 10. Whether the school has facilities for introducing and guiding graduates in employment. 11. Whether the employment status of graduates is systematically and accurately recorded, and the percentage of those employed in their specialized field. 12. The quantity, sales, storage accounting methods, and profit and loss of the value and cost of practical products. 13. Other important matters related to administration. B. Teaching and training: 1. Whether the allocation of lecture and practical training time for each subject meets the regulations. 2. Whether the lecture notes and textbooks for each subject are practical and whether new teaching materials are added at any time. 3. Whether lecture and practical training designs are closely linked. 4. Whether the practical training methods and teaching materials are practical and effective, and whether there is a system and organization. Whether all works are suitable for practical use or only for practice. 5. Whether students adopt economic principles for time and raw materials in practical training in factories and farms. Whether they do everything themselves without the help of teaching assistants, technicians, and apprentices. Whether their production skills are proficient. 6. Whether teaching pays attention to special teaching materials and the proportion they occupy. 7. Whether vacation work is implemented. How much time each student has for vacation work before graduation. How does the school assess and guide them? 8. For practical training in each subject, whether off-campus production and construction agencies are used. How do school teachers guide and assess students' off-campus practical training? 9. Whether teachers in charge of applied technology in vocational subjects have research works. 10. Whether both vocational skills subjects and theoretical subjects are able to pass. 11. Whether students are subjected to strict training, whether the school spirit is upright, whether students are diligent and studious, and how to train students' professional spirit. 12. Whether students are physically healthy and how physical education facilities are. 13. Other important matters related to teaching and training. 3. The educational administrative authorities of provinces and cities shall conduct a detailed examination of the vocational schools under their jurisdiction once a year, and report the examination results to the Ministry for record. 4. The educational administrative authorities of provinces and cities may formulate detailed measures in accordance with these key points and submit them to the Ministry for approval and implementation.

University Table Tennis Tournament: First Joint Meeting. Points to Note for Each Team

(1) The time, venue, and referees for each match will be announced in the newspaper every Wednesday.

(2) The scheduled date shall not be changed. If the date is changed due to rain or unavoidable circumstances, the association will schedule a make-up match.

(3) If the weather is not good and the suitability of the venue is uncertain, the home team should consult with the visiting team one day before the match to determine the appropriate arrangement. If the date is changed due to the unsuitability of the venue, the home team should report to the secretary of the association and try to notify the referees.

(4) The home team should be responsible for arranging the venue properly before each match (marking lines, installing net, preparing small flags for linesmen, and preparing balls for the match). Do not prepare at the last minute, which will affect the match time.

(5) The home team should be responsible for maintaining order in the match venue, but the visiting team should also fulfill its obligation to assist.

(6) The report form for each match should be obtained from the referee before the start of the match, filled out, and returned to the referee during the break after the end of the first half.

Impressions of Attending the World Games and Touring Europe: A Comprehensive View of the Football Championship

— Li Huitang

The football championship was also one of the important programs at this year's Summer Olympic Games, and the ticket revenue from the matches accounted for a superior position in the Games' financial resources. Just the last four matches at the main venue of the Games attracted nearly 400,000 spectators. The richness of the revenue can be imagined. Now the Games have become a thing of the past, and the football championship also has a destination. However, most of the information about this event is in German, and the communications we received are also brief and incomplete. Here, I will rely on my brainpower to supplement the facts I have seen, heard, and known. I believe that football fans who care about football will not be bothered and will be happy to read it.

Here, let me first tabulate the results of the All-World Football Championship (from the 3rd to the 6th) (from the 7th to the 8th) (from the 10th to the 11th) (the 15th) (Note) The third and fourth place finals were moved to Norway to defeat Poland three to two. (The 13th) × The symbol indicates overtime.

The symbol indicates that Peru originally defeated Austria four to two, but it was deemed not to comply with the current regulations, and a rematch was ordered. Peru refused to accept and eventually did not appear on the field. Austria gained the right to rematch for free.

A total of sixteen countries participated in this event. The championship was a single-elimination system. Sixteen happened to be a perfect number. No country had a bye when the draw was made. The strong teams from South America, such as Uruguay (the previous champion) and Argentina, did not send teams to participate due to conflicts with amateur rules. Only Peru came from afar. On the European side, France, the Netherlands, Spain, Czechoslovakia, Belgium, Yugoslavia, and other countries also stopped participating due to salary issues during the holidays, which reduced a lot of interest. Initially, it was hoped that 30 countries would participate, but in the end there were only 16 units. A total of 15 matches were played to find the winner of the championship.

Looking at the results and scores of the second week in the table above, there are several places where the strength gap is obvious. But it was different in the semi-finals. Almost all of the last four matches were resolved in overtime. The intensity of the match and the closeness of the strength can be imagined. Regarding the football skills of various countries, there are similar formations, and there are also different strategies. There are measures that we are accustomed to, and there are also kicking methods that are new to us. In various forms, there is indeed a need for research and learning. For example, the "third defender" formation adopted by Norway, "Third back game", is not only unimaginable in our country, but has never been seen anywhere in the eastern hemisphere. I hope that I will have free time and a good mood to write in more detail about the more interesting football strategies and the characteristics of each team, so that compatriots who care about football can jointly study the merits and demerits and perhaps improve the current level of football in our country through research. (To be continued)

The London Financial Times Praises the China Development Finance Corporation

A Central News Agency dispatch reports that the London Financial Times, a highly respected newspaper whose commentary carries considerable weight and is highly regarded by Europeans, recently published an article commenting on the China Development Finance Corporation. The Shanghai Times reprinted the article. The gist of the translation is as follows:

Since the Chinese government reformed the monetary system and stabilized exchange rates last winter, the benefits derived from this great measure are immeasurable. The recent report published by the China Development Finance Corporation is sufficient to show that the Chinese people have regained their faith in investment, and the restoration of this faith is sufficient to prove that the prospects for commerce are becoming increasingly profitable. The company was founded in 1934 with a capital of ten million yuan, raised by Chinese commercial banks and industrialists. Its purpose is to invest Chinese capital in various important enterprises, the most notable of which are railways and public utilities, which have traditionally been monopolized by foreign capital. Foreigners view this plan as an increase in the Chinese interest in investment, which is sufficient to make their bonds more stable, so there is absolutely no unwelcome psychology involved. The company's cooperation with the Sino-British Bank in June of this year to raise 1.1 million pounds for the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway loan is clear evidence of this. In addition to railways, the company's investments in public utilities include water and electricity plants, wired and wireless telegraphs, etc. Recently, as the people's confidence in the monetary system has grown stronger, in addition to lending to local governments, it has also moved to issue corporate bonds to engage in long-term lending to promote the development of industry. This is sufficient to balance the various loans and advances listed in the table, which have already increased by more than 95 million yuan, and the net profit for the previous half-year reached as much as 1.23 million yuan. Although China has various difficulties with foreign debt credit, it has made every effort to recover as a result of its recent active efforts, such as the attempt to clear the Kowloon-Canton Railway loan, which is recognized by British holders of Chinese bonds. As for the continuing development of China's internal situation as reported by the company, it is a reliable symbol of the increasingly consolidated Chinese commercial institutions.

Deadline for Industrial and Commercial Loans Approaching; Various Banks and Firms Are Accommodating; Loan Extensions Already Granted by Three Banks and Money Shops; Unpaid Interest to Be Recovered from Hengxing and Henglai Money Shops

The end of October deadline for long-term industrial and commercial credit loans in Shanghai is fast approaching. The factories, companies, and shops that have taken out these loans have begun to contact the various banks and money shops to negotiate extension procedures. The Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and the Central Bank are allowing extensions for loans to the various money shops and are recovering unpaid interest from the two money shops. Details are as follows:

Handling of End-of-October Procedures by Banks and Money Shops

The total amount of long-term credit loans borrowed by various companies, shops, and factories in Shanghai from banks and money shops with an end-of-October deadline is over 50 million yuan. Shanghai remittance money shops account for six-tenths of this amount, Ningbo and Hankou money shops account for three-tenths, and commercial banks account for one-tenth. Borrowers are now separately contacting the various banks and money shops to negotiate extension procedures. Banks and money shops will specially accommodate those with better credit and grant them extensions. At the same time, they will also provide new credit loans. It is widely expected that this year's end of October will be very different from previous years and can be safely passed. As for the money market's foreign exchange borrowing, yesterday it was eight points, which proves that the money supply is not tight.

Loan Extensions Granted Again by Money Shops

The Ministry of Finance previously established a Supervisory Committee to assist the money shops and allocated 25 million yuan in financial public bonds for borrowing from the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, the Central Bank, and the reserve of various commercial banks and money shops. The borrowing money shops have now returned the loans one after another. Only a few money shops, such as Hengxing and Henglai, still have over 10 million yuan outstanding, which has been repeatedly extended and has not yet been repaid. The Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and the Central Bank have agreed to extend the repayment period again. However, the amount borrowed by the Hengxing and Henglai money shops is over 5 million yuan, and their collateral is real estate. Because these two money shops have started handling accounts receivable this year, they have delayed paying the interest due. The Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and the Central Bank have now notified the Money Shop Supervisory Committee to recover the money from the two money shops.

Shanghai Municipal Police Department Orders All District Stations to Conduct a General Mobilization to Suppress Opium Smokers; Over 80 Opium Dens Busted in One Month; Expansion of Temporary Hospital to Be Realized Soon

According to the Dagu News Agency, the Shanghai Municipal Police Department has already started a general mobilization to suppress opium smokers in the city. Each district has busted over 80 opium dens and plans to expand the drug addiction treatment center to accommodate registered opium smokers as much as possible. The details are as follows:

General Mobilization Throughout the City

Since the conclusion of the citywide general inspection work for banning opium and drugs in the city, the Shanghai Municipal Police Department, in order to strictly enforce the city's prohibition policy, has specially ordered all its subordinate districts to transfer senior police officers from each district, together with investigators from the Fourth Section of the General Bureau, to implement a general mobilization, house-by-house, to suppress opium smokers, starting from October 1. They will also be stationed on various roads, and if they see anyone who looks like they are smoking opium or drugs, they will immediately stop them for questioning and send them to a nearby designated or special hospital for examination.

Various Districts Bust Opium Dens

The Shanghai Municipal Police Department fears that some lawless elements within the concession are not only smoking opium with permits, but also privately setting up opium dens for others to smoke, which is a major obstacle to the promotion of the prohibition policy. Therefore, it has strictly ordered all districts to seriously investigate and suppress them. Currently, it is estimated that since September 10, over 80 cases of privately set up opium dens have been busted throughout the city. There have also been many cases of trafficking and smoking red pills, morphine, heroin, and other drugs, which have been transferred to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for punishment according to the law.

Accommodating Registered Opium Smokers

There are a total of over 30 designated or special drug addiction treatment hospitals. Those sent directly by the Shanghai Municipal Police Department for treatment and those sentenced by the Songhu Garrison Headquarters and sent to the Longhua and Zhabei drug addiction treatment centers are all full, and it is impossible to accommodate any more. However, the Shanghai Municipal Police Department has received an unusually enthusiastic response from opium smokers applying for voluntary drug addiction treatment in recent days. They are sent for treatment in order of application, but it is still insufficient. Therefore, in order to help opium smokers get rid of their suffering as soon as possible, the bureau is negotiating with the city's Anti-Opium Committee and other related agencies to plan the expansion and establishment of temporary drug addiction treatment centers and to increase the number of special hospitals in order to accommodate opium smokers as much as possible. This plan should be implemented soon.

Ministry of Railways Orders Two Railway Administrations to Strictly Prevent Smuggling

In order to facilitate the transportation and sale of legitimate goods, the Beijing-Shanghai and Ningbo-Hangzhou-Shanghai Railway Administrations received an order from the Ministry of Railways on September 3, No. 3775, stating that the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce had sent a telegram on behalf of the association, stating that at the sixth regular meeting of the Smuggling Inspection Committee of the association on the 21st of this month, the director of the inspection team proposed that since the government's vigorous anti-smuggling efforts, smuggling by sea vessels and railways had gradually disappeared, but smugglers were increasingly transporting smuggled goods to the interior by civilian boats, small steamers, tugboats, or long-distance buses to avoid inspection. The anti-smuggling agencies in various places have not yet paid attention to this. At present, due to anti-smuggling efforts, the transportation and sale of legitimate goods to various places are often hindered by inspectors, and they are detained for no reason, which hinders commerce. Please find a way to provide relief. It was agreed that this matter should be ordered by the Ministry of Railways to anti-smuggling agencies in various places to pay attention to civilian boats, small steamers, highway trucks, and prevent smuggling. At the same time, inspectors should be warned that they must facilitate the transportation and sale of legitimate goods and must not detain them arbitrarily. After discussion, it was decided to pass the proposal and telegraph the Ministry of Railways for review and implementation. The regulations on the inspection of imported goods and the transportation and sale of goods clearly stipulate the goods that should be inspected when loaded on ships, civilian boats, cars, and trains. The current inspection methods are very clear and should be earnestly implemented. Inspectors should also not arbitrarily detain the transportation and sale of legitimate goods, causing trouble. In addition to the distribution, the request should be reviewed and implemented in accordance with the instructions. This order is hereby issued to inform all departments.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Asks Guangdong Province to Abolish Tobacco Monopoly and Implement Uniform Tax System

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating that on the 5th of this month, the Guangdong Provincial Tobacco Industry Association sent a letter stating that since Chen's dictatorship in Guangdong Province, the implementation of the native tobacco monopoly has caused difficulties for merchants and farmers. The association has repeatedly reported this matter. On the 16th of this month, they suddenly received an announcement from Song, the Guangdong Finance Commissioner, and Wang, the director of the Stamp Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau, stating that in order to relieve tobacco farmers and reorganize tax revenue, they decided to continue the native tobacco monopoly. They were shocked and confused. Lending loans to tobacco farmers is a common lending practice. Whether there is a monopoly or not, the government can lend money at any time. If the original interest rate is too high, it can also be ordered to restrict it and prohibit high interest rates. It is not necessary to implement a monopoly to relieve tobacco farmers. Regarding tax revenue, the Ministry of Finance has clear regulations that are universally implemented in all provinces. There are rules and regulations to follow, and it is not necessary to have a monopoly to reorganize tax revenue. Moreover, the native tobacco monopoly hides taxes in prices, which are the highest in the country. The higher the price, the slower the sales, the more storage, and the more smuggling. Restricting production will cause tobacco farmers to lose their jobs. Continuing the monopoly will cause tobacco merchants to go out of business. In recent months, the business sales have plummeted, and hundreds of thousands of people have lost their jobs. Their suffering can be seen. If the monopoly is maintained, the tobacco farmers will not be widely benefited, and the merchants who have been deprived of their livelihoods and gone bankrupt have been severely damaged. In this case, both tobacco farmers and tobacco merchants will suffer losses, and the government's tax revenue will not be helped. The advantages and disadvantages of this are clear. Moreover, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek has spoken out against the implementation of monopolistic operations competing with the people for profit, and there have been announcements of the cancellation of harsh and miscellaneous taxes. This kind of native tobacco monopoly that harms the people has not been implemented throughout the country. How can Guangdong be treated especially harshly and used as a testing ground for the monopoly? Merchants and others are waiting to be relieved of their suffering and are exhausted. They dare to express their feelings and appeal again and again, hoping that the Ministry of Finance will uphold justice and quickly abolish the harsh monopoly policy, so that the merchants and farmers in the entire province will be grateful. The association checked and found that the Ministry of Finance had already changed the tobacco and alcohol monopoly system in various provinces to a fixed tax in order to unify the tax system and rectify tax revenue. However, Guangdong Province has its own customs, using the name of a monopoly and implementing heavy taxes. Before the province had accepted the delegation, although farmers and merchants were in difficulty, they could still claim that there was no way to appeal. If this kind of harmful policy is left after the unification of government orders and the elimination of annoying policies, it will inevitably make tobacco merchants lose hope and feel resentful. Native tobacco is not comparable to salt, and there is no need for a monopoly. All provinces implement the fixed tax method, and Guangdong Province should not continue to be different, so that the Ministry of Finance's facilities for unifying the tax system over the years will have a sense of unfinished business. It is appropriate to telegraph the Ministry of Finance for review and approval, and it would be convenient to handle the matter as requested by the association. Shanghai Chamber of Commerce.

Tea Exports Decline This Year; Soviet Russia's Tea Planting Can Be Self-Sufficient; the Way to Recover Is to Improve the Manufacturing Method

According to tea industry sources, the tea industry has been declining in recent years, and this year it is even more bleak. Foreign sales markets have been seized by Japanese tea, Ceylon tea, Siamese tea, and others. Soviet Russia was one of the largest sales markets for Chinese tea, but now it has also opened its own tea farms and is planting extensively, which can achieve self-sufficiency. However, according to the tea industry, Chinese tea has a unique color, aroma, and taste. If the manufacturing method and tea farms can be reformed, a portion of the foreign market may be recovered.

Various Silk Factories Will Not Stop Production for the Time Being, but the Future of Silk Sales Is Still Bleak

The Dagong News Agency reports that recently, the Shanghai silk market has seen firm silk prices due to the poor autumn cocoon harvest in the silk-producing areas of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, poor reeling, and estimates that the cocoon cost cannot be low. However, silk sales remain weak. Yesterday, the European and American silk markets remained calm, but the spot price in the Yokohama silk market opened at 755 yuan, an increase of 5 yuan compared to the previous day, and the forward price was 732 yuan, an increase of 3 yuan. The price of Shanghai Zhengji white filature silk in the Lyon silk market rose by 18 francs per kilo, opening at 84 francs, but there were no transactions due to price differences. Currently, there are still 41 silk factories in operation in the Hongkou, Zhabei, and Xinzha districts of Shanghai. The daily output is up to 30 dan of white filature silk. However, due to the stagnation of exports and domestic sales, the future of the silk industry is quite pessimistic. According to silk factory sources, although the output of various factories is very slow, they will not stop production for the time being because there are still many cocoons in storage.

Jiangxi Asks the Ministry of Railways to Reduce Agricultural Product Transportation Charges to Recover Interests and Relieve the Rural Areas

Jiangxi Province has had a bumper harvest of agricultural products this year. The Jiangxi Provincial Agricultural Product Transportation and Sales Agency seems to be dissatisfied with the freight rates on the Zhejiang-Jiangxi and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways. Therefore, it hopes that the Ministry of Railways will find a way to reduce the rates in order to recover interests and relieve the rural economy. According to the Jiangxi Provincial Transportation and Sales Agency in Shanghai, Jiangxi's agricultural product output is very high every year. Items such as miscellaneous grains, yarn cloth, and porcelain are quite large. The distribution of these products is centered on Shanghai. Before the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway was opened to traffic, the transportation of these agricultural products out of the province was all by water, passing through Jiujiang and other places to Shanghai, which took eight or nine days. The Yangtze River ships are controlled by foreign ships, and the annual leakage of water feet is not small. Since the opening of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, it has greatly increased the convenience of transporting goods from Jiangxi to Shanghai. However, because the railway freight charges seem to be more expensive than water transport, except for more expensive items such as cotton yarn and cloth, which are transported by rail, other miscellaneous grains and other items are still mostly transported by water. Jiangxi has had a bumper harvest of miscellaneous grains such as rice, wheat, and rapeseed this year. Transportation and sales will be even more enthusiastic. Therefore, it is hoped that the railway authorities will reduce the freight charges for agricultural products from Jiangxi on the Zhejiang-Jiangxi and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, so that water transport can be changed to land transport, which can not only recover interests but also relieve the rural economy.

Parcels Sent to France Should Fill in Detailed Tax Declaration Lists

Shanghai Postal Administration Notice No. 1356 states that according to Circular No. 9721269 of August 5 of this year from the International Postal Union, the French Post Office sent a letter stating that the French Customs had received complaints that the tax declaration lists (i.e., Form No. PC-3) attached to parcels sent from various countries were not detailed enough. The gross weight, net weight, and value of each item in the parcel were often not specified in the list. Sometimes the "What's Inside" column of the list was vaguely filled in with words such as "local products." As a result, when the customs authorities examined the contents and their weight, it was difficult to open all the parcels, which would easily cause delays. It was also found that some parcels were detained by the customs authorities because they did not have a certificate or import license, or because the permit was mistakenly sent to the initial receiving exchange office in the country without direct customs. This notice is hereby issued to inform everyone. Director Zha Peilin, October 5.

Customs Provides 900 Yuan in Compensation; Maritime Court Determines Shooting Was Due to Circumstances

Datong News Agency reports: On January 13th of this year, the No. 25 "Xunxing" patrol ship of the Shanghai Customs sank the "Jin Wanli" fishing boat in the Zhushanmen waters of Zhejiang, killing fisherman Lou Ahe. Afterwards, the deceased's family repeatedly appealed to the Ningbo Tongxiang Association for negotiations. Subsequently, the Customs convened a temporary maritime court to investigate the truth of the case. At that time, the judgment concluded that the Xunxing patrol ship had repeatedly ordered the fishing boat to stop, but the Jin Wanli refused to obey. Therefore, the Xunxing patrol ship's warning shot was indeed compelled by the circumstances and found no fault. However, 900 yuan was granted as a compassionate allowance to the deceased to show sympathy. After the Customs reported the above judgment to the Customs Department of the Ministry of Finance, it was learned yesterday that the Customs Department had already issued the compensation to the deceased's widow, Lou Xu, who received it with a guarantee. The case has now come to an end.

China Merchants Bureau Supplies Bidding; Successful Bidders Sign Contracts

Since its reorganization, the state-run China Merchants Bureau has strictly adopted open bidding procedures for all purchases by relevant departments as much as possible. Ordinary products have a large annual expenditure. As per usual ordinary practice, the general affairs department is responsible for purchasing them. This is not only frequent, but the procedures are extremely complicated, and even if the handling is meticulous, it cannot demonstrate great impartiality. Therefore, it was decided to reform this habit and publicly invite bids for the required ordinary goods, categorized by type. Bids were opened in public on the 22nd of last month, and senior officials designated by the Bureau reviewed the bids. For printing, the lowest bid was 83% by Daya Jiwu Institute. For tea, the lowest price was offered by Run Chang Tea House. For other supplies, such as toilet paper and matches, the lowest price was offered by De Tai Hao. All were selected as successful bidders, and the Bureau immediately notified them to complete the contract signing procedures. For stationery, only China Bookstore submitted a bid, with a bid price of 15%. It is heard that the China Merchants Bureau considers this bid price to be quite appropriate, so it has decided to negotiate the lowest price with China Bookstore based on this bid price and have China Bookstore handle all stationery supplies. The bids for soap, towels, batteries, etc., were found to be slightly higher than the wholesale prices of the original manufacturers, so the Bureau did not adopt them and decided to contact the manufacturers directly for purchases. According to the person in charge of the Bureau, this decision to openly bid for ordinary supplies will save approximately 15% to 20%.

Deputy Section Chief of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, Wang Qiguang, Framed; Someone Sends Letter Implicating Him in the Xuansheng Case; Released After Investigation

Wang Qiguang, deputy section chief of the Xihu section of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Bureau, was suddenly taken to the court by a prosecutor from the Shanghai Local Court, accompanied by inspectors and bailiffs from the Public Security Bureau, at 9 PM the day before yesterday. The Shanghai Public Security Bureau cracked the case and arrested the suspects Wang Zhensheng, Mao Yonghu, Jin Daohong, Zhao Yunhong, and the women Wang Zai and Zhang Mo. After confirming their confessions, they were transferred to the local court and detained separately. Unexpectedly, the day before yesterday, a letter was delivered to the detention center, addressed to one of the detainees in the case. The letter said that arrangements had been made and asked for pocket money to be collected from the section chief at No. 50 Pu Bai Fang, Luban Road in the French Concession. After inspecting the letter, the detention center deemed the matter extremely important and reported it to the chief prosecutor. The chief prosecutor also considered it a major matter and immediately sent a prosecutor to the French Concession police station along with inspectors from the Shanghai Public Security Bureau to search No. 50 Pu Bai Fang. They found nothing. After inquiry, it was learned that the address was the private residence of Wang Qiguang, deputy section chief of the Xihu section. They then rushed to the Railway Bureau and arrested Wang. The detainees were interrogated overnight, but none of them knew Wang. Therefore, the occurrence of this incident must be a prank by Wang Qiguang's enemy who saw the news report of this relatively important case and deliberately created this farcical drama. Otherwise, if it were a major criminal, how could he voluntarily throw himself into the net and send a letter to the court? Cattle Disease in This City; Dairy Cow Competition Postponed; Aim is to Improve Domestic Breeds; Cattle Breeding Ground in Chuansha

The first dairy cow competition organized by the Livestock Improvement Promotion Association of this city was originally scheduled to be held on the 4th of this month, but has now been postponed due to a new disease recently affecting dairy cows in the city's dairies. A reporter from Datong News Agency inquired with the Association about the situation, as follows:

Reason for Postponement: Since initiating the first dairy cow competition in Shanghai, the Association has received assistance from Cai Wuji, Director of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, and Wang Zhaoyi, Chief of the Animal Inspection Section of the Municipal Health Bureau, and preparations have proceeded smoothly. Registration for both domestic and foreign dairy cows participating in the competition has reached one hundred heads. However, recently, some cattle in Shanghai dairies have developed a disease. Although whether it is contagious is still under investigation, the Association has temporarily decided to postpone the event for the sake of caution and to prevent transmission.

Purpose of Competition: The purpose of the dairy cow competition initiated by the Association is to improve the breeds of dairy cows in our country. Therefore, when the competition is held, dairy cattle breeders and farmers from all over the country will be invited to Shanghai to visit. At the same time, it is planned to establish a dairy cattle breeding ground in Chuansha County to improve the local dairy cattle breeds, so that the milk production and milk quality of domestic dairy cows can be improved at an accelerated rate. In this era, when milk has been recognized by the public as the main nutrient, preventing the leakage of nutrients is undoubtedly important.

Shocking Rumors Spread; Carefree Old Man; Seventy-Seven Years Old, Traveling Around the World Seventeen Times

Mr. Blightle Bank, an American, is seventy-seven years old. He used to be a businessman. At the age of fifty, he bought government bonds with all his life savings and no longer engaged in business, traveling at will for his own enjoyment, because he had loved traveling since he was a child. His only son is now running a real estate business in New York, so Mr. White is completely free and carefree. He can leave whenever he wants. In the past twenty years, he has traveled around the world sixteen times, covering a journey of one million miles. Fifty years ago, he first decided to come to China, and now he is making his seventeenth round-the-world trip and arrived in Shanghai a few days ago. Mr. White prepares $3,000 in travel expenses each time he travels. When the funds are about to run out, he plans to return. His itinerary is uncertain, like idle clouds out of the mountains, going wherever he likes. He does not stay long in each place, enjoying the scenery, watching dramas, or attending art exhibitions. When he is tired, he packs his bags and goes elsewhere. Mr. White does not like to travel by plane, not because he is old, but because he believes that traveling should be leisurely and comfortable, and rushing is uninteresting. Mr. White always likes to go and witness it when a country is about to have major events. He still remembers being in Washington when the American Civil War ended, and being in Russia during the Russo-Japanese War, watching the Russian fleet sail out and being defeated by the Japanese. In 1911, he first saw the Chinese Revolution, the Balkan War, and left the country just before the border was blockaded. When the European War broke out, he happened to be in Germany. There are too many other things to mention. Although Mr. White's spirit is good, he admits that his ambition is not as good as in the past, and he does not want to go to places with many troubles, so after he arrived in Shanghai, the tense situation between China and Japan eased slightly, which Mr. White found very enjoyable. Mr. White once said that among the countries he has visited, the most impressive is China, and the changes in China in recent years are indeed amazing. If his physical strength permits in the future, he will continue to travel frequently to enjoy his old age. Mr. White left Shanghai yesterday for Hong Kong and will go to Manila and other places. Eventually, he will also visit Jerusalem and then return home via Europe.

First Special Court Continues Hearing of the American-Chinese Bank Lawsuit; Many Responsible Persons Evade Appearance; Liquidator Reports Confusing Accounts

Shareholders of the failed American-Chinese Bank, such as Gu Yubo, and the initiators of the Daxin Bank, the predecessor of the American-Chinese Bank, such as Shen Jingzhong, were sued by more than a dozen creditors of the American-Chinese Bank, such as Wang Tingfang, to the First Special District Court for fraud and embezzlement. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Huang Risheng continued to hold a joint hearing. The defendants, including Sun Wenkui and Wang Zhonglin, reported to the court with their defense lawyer Lin Yingqing. At this time, lawyer Ma Lewu represented the creditor Li Jingfang to the court, stating his participation in the lawsuit. After verification by Judge Huang, it was announced that the cases would be rescheduled for further hearing on the afternoon of the 19th of this month.

Criminals Call for Improved Detention Conditions; Four Deaths in One Night; Two-Thirds Suffer from Illness; List Four Goals for Improvement

Since Shanghai County cracked down on smoking, the Public Security Bureau's detention center has suddenly increased a large number of smoking offenders, but the detention center's equipment and management have not been expanded, so there are inevitable problems of crowding and inadequacy. From 5 to 6 PM on September 30, four people died of illness in a row. Among the smoking offenders in the detention center, those who are sick account for more than two-thirds. The authorities have not seen any preventive measures. Therefore, the detainees Wang Haimen, Tang Jinxiang, Gu Guanlin, and others, 64 smoking offenders in total, jointly submitted a petition to the county party department, requesting relief, and listed the points that should be improved, such as (1) moldy rice and many people are poisoned, (2) unboiled drinking water leads to bloating, (3) too little "release" time and no opportunity for walking and exercise, (4) those with diseases are not isolated, and the spread of infection is increasing. In the petition, it says that the people have occasionally violated the law, but the case is not theft, and it does not seem that they should be subjected to such abuse. At the 159th meeting of the county party department yesterday, it was considered that the petition was true and decided to send a letter to the county government to order the Public Security Bureau to earnestly improve it to prevent recurrence.

Roads Like a Tiger's Mouth - Not Easy to Walk in Shanghai - 327 Pedestrians Injured in August

The Public Works Bureau's Police Department announced the following statistics for the number of people injured and killed in various vehicle accidents in August of this year:

Number of Injuries and Deaths: In August of this year, a total of 327 pedestrians, passengers, and rickshaw drivers were injured in vehicle accidents. The number of deaths due to injuries was 12. The highest number of accidents occurred with bicycles, with 71 pedestrians injured, followed by private cars, with 60 pedestrians injured (including three seriously injured) and one death. Next were rickshaws, freight carts, etc. As for passengers and rickshaw drivers injured and killed, rickshaw accidents were the most numerous, with 59 rickshaw passengers injured and three deaths in August, followed by bicycles, with 25 injured, one seriously injured, and one death.

Calling for Prevention: After investigation by the Police Department, 85 injured people were children under the age of 16, with 3 deaths. Therefore, it is very dangerous for children to walk on the road, and parents should pay close attention to this to avoid accidents. In addition to drawing yellow lines at road intersections to facilitate pedestrians crossing the road, the Police Department has also hired two lecturers to give lectures on "Safety First When Walking" in teahouses and factories every day. A total of 156 lectures were held in August, with more than 6,640 listeners.

Widow Sues Father-in-Law - Abandonment and Encroachment Case - Judge Urges Reconciliation

Zhou Zuohong, a native of Chaozhou, runs Zhenfeng and other pawnshops at 19 Taopeng Road and other locations. His son, Zhou Huiqi, after graduating from Fudan University, went to teach at the Chinese School in Mahua, Nanyang. He returned to Shanghai in a certain year and married Weng Wenying, the daughter of the owner of Shengxing Pawnshop at 8 Maohai Road (a graduate of the Patriotic Girls' School, currently studying medicine at Tongde Medical College). However, less than eight months after the marriage, Zhou Huiqi died of illness. When Zhou died, Weng Wenying was pregnant and subsequently gave birth to a daughter. Recently, Weng Wenying sued Zhou Huiyi in the Special First Court for encroachment, alleging that her husband had remitted 1,300 yuan to his brother, Zhou Huiyi, before his death, but Zhou Huiyi refused to hand it over. The details of the trial have been reported in this newspaper. Now, Weng Wenying, represented by lawyer Qiu Hanping, filed a lawsuit against her father-in-law, Zhou Zuohong, in the Special First Court for abandonment and encroachment, alleging that Zhou Zuohong stopped paying living expenses after her husband's death, and that 1,000 yuan remitted by her husband from Mahua during his lifetime was deposited with Zhou Zuohong at his Zhenchang Pawnshop, but has not been returned. She requested that he be punished according to Articles 294 and 335 of the Criminal Code and also filed a civil lawsuit, demanding repayment of the deposit of 1,000 yuan and interest at the statutory rate of 5% per annum from July 1 of the year 19 until the date of execution, and ordering the payment of alimony of 12,000 yuan, as well as a deposit of 9,000 yuan for education funds, with the principal and interest to be used for the education expenses of the young daughter. Yesterday afternoon, this case was heard in the Criminal Division Eight by Judge Chuan Lin. According to Weng Wenying's testimony, after her husband's death, the defendant's family regarded her as an unlucky person. Because the child she gave birth to was a girl, the defendant held a patriarchal attitude and treated her extremely cruelly. As a result, she attempted suicide once and returned to her mother's home, while continuing her studies at Tongde Medical College in order to support herself in the future. However, since her husband's death, the defendant has not provided any living expenses, so she filed the lawsuit. Questioning Zhou Zuohong, he testified that he had not neglected the plaintiff's life, and had rented a front building next door to the Di family at a monthly rent of 18 yuan, which has not yet been returned, and that he also paid 200-300 yuan a year for the plaintiff's education expenses, but the plaintiff demanded 960 yuan, which he could not afford. He also retained lawyers Zou Yu and Chen Changsheng to defend him. Judge Chuan believed that this case was a family dispute, and that the amount in dispute was not significant, so reconciliation was the best way to avoid litigation. He adjourned the hearing and ordered the parties to attempt reconciliation outside the court.

Ningxing Discussion - Young Man Jumps into the Sea and Commits Suicide - Leaping into the River at Zhanghuabang - Deceased Ye Zhixing Left a Suicide Note

The Ningxing Wheel, operated by Sanbei Company on the Shanghai-Ningbo route, departed from Shanghai for Ningbo on the 3rd. Before it had left the Wusongkou, a passenger jumped into the sea and committed suicide. The following are the details explored by a reporter from Datong News Agency:

Jumping into the River to Commit Suicide

The Ningxing Wheel departed from Shanghai at 5 p.m. on the date. At about 7 p.m. that evening, while passing through Zhanghuabang (before leaving the Wusongkou), a young (approximately 20 years old) passenger on the upper bunk of the ship jumped into the sea and committed suicide. The tea attendant Dai A Yao, who was responsible for entertaining the passengers, immediately reported to the shipowner, who stopped the ship to salvage the body. However, it had already been submerged by the tide and could not be recovered. The ship then continued its voyage to Ningbo.

Suicide Note Recovered

Afterwards, tea attendant Dai A Yao recovered a felt hat, a long gown, and a suicide note from the passenger's berth. The suicide note was written in blue ink and was addressed to the tea attendant. The words were as follows: "Brother A Yao, I came here to commit suicide. Please send my hat and long gown to Mr. Shi Hexuan of Quanquan Factory, 36 Lane, Tongzhou Road, Hongkou, No. 2. There are more than a few yuan in my pocket as a reward for your trouble. Whether you send it or not depends on your conscience." Signed "Ye Zhiyu." Presumably, this is the name of the deceased. After the ship arrived in Shanghai yesterday, the tea attendant delivered the suicide note and belongings to the address according to the instructions.

Robbing Puxin Town - One Thief Arrested in Shanghai - Principal Arrives in Court to Testify - Sentenced to be Transferred to Qingpu for Trial

At about 5 p.m. on August 23, Xin Town Township, Qingpu County, was attacked by a large number of Anhui bandits, more than 40 in number, each armed with long and short guns. They first emptied the township's defense post of weapons, and then began robbing shops of property worth more than 4,000 yuan, before shouting and boarding a boat to escape. The day before yesterday, Li Quanwu, the detective chief of the local water patrol team, received a tip that a member of the gang, Xu Mojian (age 58), from Anhui Province, was hiding at 30 Renchang Lane, Qiwupu Road, in the Public Concession. He came to Shanghai to report to the Yulin Road Police Station for assistance in the arrest. The detective chief dispatched detective Pan Yunlong to arrest him at the address, and brought him and his 17-year-old grandson, Xu Daoshi, to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the First Criminal Court of the First Special District. Lawyer Zhang Shizhu from the Public Works Bureau described the case and stated that the defense post and the robbed shops were present to identify them, and agreed to the transfer. Li Quanwu, the water patrol captain, submitted a public notice. Hu Zhangshu, a soldier from the defense post, from Anhui Province, stated that he heard gunfire at the time and saw a crowd of thirty or forty bandits. They tied him up with ropes and beat him, and the weapons were also taken away. The defendant Xu Mojian was one of them. Shen Shasan, the owner of the Xieshun distiller from Qingpu, testified that he was taken out of the workshop by several bandits, tied up on the bandit ship, and beaten. They also demanded 50 yuan for passage fees. The property in the distillery was robbed, and he had no money left. He begged his captors to release him. He witnessed Xu Mojian carrying a large bag of copper coins for the first time, and cigarettes and other items into the ship for the second time. He was not falsely accusing him. When questioned, Xu Mojian denied everything. Judge Zhong Qing ordered that Xu Mojian be handed over to Li Quanwu, an official from the Qingpu County Government, for removal. The grandson, Xu Daoshi, did not need to be transferred.

Brother and Sister Argue over Smoking - Brother Commits Suicide by Taking Poison

Wu Fuhui, a native of Ningbo, 36 years old, residing at 11 Quanyuli, Anaqin Road, in the French Concession, is a businessman. His son, Yue Lang, 19 years old, does nothing and hangs out with hooligans every day. At 10 a.m. on the 4th, Yue Lang was criticized by his sister, Lin Lang (21 years old), for consuming cigarettes and not producing anything, and for losing money every day on cigarettes. This led to a conflict and argument between the siblings. Later, Yue Lang went out and did not return. He committed suicide by purchasing raw opium and swallowing it. At 10 a.m. the next morning, he returned home. Because the poison took effect, he was extremely uncomfortable and his face turned pale. His mother, Wu Zhou, discovered this and sent him to Renji Hospital. However, he was too deeply poisoned to be saved and died at 1:40 p.m. The hospital reported to the French Police, who sent detectives to investigate. The body was sent to the Tongren Funeral Home for examination. Yesterday, a report was submitted to the Second Special Court. The chief prosecutor and forensic medical officer arrived and confirmed that the deceased had indeed died from poisoning before death. After questioning the deceased's mother and sister, they ordered the body to be handed over to the deceased's mother, Wu Zhou, for burial.

Young Child Suffers from Dysentery - Skin Ulcerates After Taking Medicine - Tang Liwen Sues Female Doctor Zhang Xiuyu - Experimented in Court Once and Injured

Tang Liwen, from Zhenjiang, residing at 450, 391 Lane, Jiangjia Lane, Gordon Road, sought treatment at the Labor Hospital on Xiaoshadu Road for his two-year-old son, Da Shizi, who was suffering from dysentery. Female doctor Zhang Xiuyu of the hospital diagnosed him and gave him five packets of medicine powder and a bottle of sesame oil, instructing him to take the medicine powder in five doses and then swallow the sesame oil. However, after taking the medicine powder, the child immediately vomited it out. The skin and flesh where the vomit passed became ulcerated. After being sent to Baojiang Hospital, the diagnosis was that the medicine powder contained toxic substances. Tang retained a lawyer and filed a lawsuit in the Special First Court against Dr. Zhang for negligent injury. The Special Court had already heard the case once. Zhang Xiuyu stated that the medicine did not contain any toxic substances, and that the child also suffered from stomatitis, with sleeping symptoms already present in the mouth and many white spots on the lips. The court ordered that the diagnosis report from Lu Baojiang Hospital be reviewed later. Yesterday afternoon, this case was heard again in Criminal Division Eight by Judge Chuan Lin. The diagnosis report from Baojiang Hospital had also been submitted to the case file. The details stated in the report were entirely based on the statements of both parties. After being distributed to the lawyers of both parties for review, Judge Chuan applied the so-called toxic medicine powder presented by the plaintiff, mixed with sesame oil, to Tang Da Shizi's arm to see if there was indeed a possibility of ulceration. However, after a considerable amount of time, no such phenomenon was observed. Subsequently, a doctor named Sha arrived in court and testified about the diagnosis and treatment of Tang Da Shizi's stomatitis. The court then ordered the start of the debate. After the lawyers of both parties debated, Judge Fu announced the conclusion of the hearing and scheduled the judgment for 2 p.m. on the 8th.

The Xingye Trust Company Sponsors the Opening of the Health Assurance Society

According to Xin Sheng She (New Sound News Agency), the Shanghai Health Assurance Society, sponsored by the Municipal Xingye Trust Company, is scheduled to open this morning. Details are as follows:

Opening This Morning

The society has been in preparation for over four months. Its purpose is purely to enhance the health of citizens. Specialist doctors have been hired to provide free medical consultations to members. The opening is scheduled for this morning without any ceremony. In the afternoon, tours will be offered to various sectors. According to the person in charge of the society, speaking to a Xin Sheng She reporter yesterday, "A sound mind resides in a sound body. In this era of the survival of the fittest, if we wish for the survival of the entire nation, there is no alternative to self-strengthening. The first condition for self-strengthening is that every citizen must have a healthy body. Therefore, the national budgets of Japan and Soviet Russia both include huge allocations for national health policies. This shows that their path to becoming strong nations lies in their approach to national strength. The weakness of our nation is an undeniable fact. Although there has been considerable progress in recent years, compared to other strong nations, the progress is clearly insufficient. The reasons for this are, firstly, that health construction requires multi-faceted efforts that cannot be achieved in a short time, and secondly, that social and economic instability causes everyone to worry about food and clothing, which invisibly hinders the essential elements of national self-strengthening. The Shanghai Xingye Trust Company, in view of this, has specially established the Health Assurance Society in a municipal capacity. By charging the most economical and reasonable membership fees, it seeks citizen membership. Actively, it will contribute various forms of health knowledge to members, enabling them to know how to enter the path of health. Passively, it has specially hired various well-known specialist doctors to provide free diagnosis and treatment to members, restoring their lost health."

Overview of Society Affairs

(1) This society is established by the Shanghai Xingye Trust Company and will be managed with the spirit of the Xingye Trust Company in operating other social enterprises. (2) The society's membership is divided into two types: basic and special. The annual membership fee for basic members is three yuan, and for special members, it is ten yuan. Although there is a difference in fees, the society's services are provided by specialist doctors who provide conscientious diagnosis and guidance, without any discrimination. However, special members have a special waiting room and the right to advance their consultation time. (3) Group memberships (such as for institutions, schools, shops, factories, etc.) will receive the following discounts: 10% off the original membership fee for 10 or more people, 15% off for 50 or more people, 20% off for 100 or more people, and further negotiations are possible for 150 or more people. (4) For family memberships, each family member other than the head of the household will pay half of the head of household's membership fee. (5) Each of the society's major specialties is headed by highly experienced and reputable medical doctors. Their names and consultation hours are listed separately below. In addition to the specialist doctors who are on duty during designated hours, the society also has doctors on duty who provide continuous service during consultation hours. Consultation hours are from 8:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 2:00 PM to 7:00 PM. The clinic is closed on Sundays and holidays. (6) The society is not only established for treating illnesses but will also plan to hold health trips, group check-ups, and other health campaigns from time to time, as well as publish materials that instill health knowledge to enhance the health and happiness of its members. (7) The society has special maternity insurance certificates. Each certificate costs a set fee and covers all costs, regardless of normal or difficult delivery, hospitalization, or injections. This novel approach solves the entire labor and delivery problem for pregnant women. The certificates are divided into three types: A, B, and C, which can be pre-ordered according to their economic situation. For detailed information, please contact the society. (8) The general rules for the treatment of society members can be obtained from the society or the Shanghai Xingye Trust Company.

Treatment Guidelines

After the society found its address at 65 Muir Road, it began recruiting members and formulated treatment guidelines for members. The original text is as follows: Article 1: Any citizen who voluntarily joins the society and pays the membership fee in accordance with the regulations shall be a member of the society. Article 2: The society's membership is divided into two types: basic members and special members. The membership fees are listed on the left: Basic members pay three yuan per person per year in national currency, and special members pay ten yuan per person per year in national currency. Article 3: To become a member, one must first fill out the application form provided by the society, along with the membership fee, and submit it to the society. The society will then issue an official receipt and membership card. Article 4: The society's membership card is valid for one year from the date of issuance. Article 5: Groups of ten or more people, such as institutions, schools, factories, and shops, may join the society as members in the name of the group. Article 6: Group membership fees shall be handled in accordance with Article 2, but they shall enjoy the following preferential treatment: 10% off for ten or more people, 15% off for fifty or more people, 20% off for one hundred or more people, and further negotiations for one hundred and fifty or more people. The group name must be added above the member's name on the group membership card to indicate the difference. Article 7: For family memberships, each family member other than the head of the household will pay half of the head of household's membership fee. Article 8: Society members may come to the society for free outpatient treatment if they are ill, but they must bring their membership card to register. No registration fee will be charged. Article 9: The society's outpatient hours are from 8:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 2:00 PM to 7:00 PM every day. The clinic is closed on Sundays and holidays. Registration hours for house calls are the same as for outpatient visits. Anyone requesting a house call outside of registration hours will be considered an emergency. Article 10: The society has specially opened a waiting room for special members and a waiting room for basic members to facilitate separate waiting. Article 11: To facilitate members' dispensing of medicine, the society has specially established a dispensing department to serve members at low drug prices. Article 12: The society's specialist doctors preside over each department within the prescribed time. Regardless of whether they are special members or basic members, they will be diagnosed by doctors in each department, but special members have the right to receive priority diagnosis. Article 13: If various major and minor surgeries are required for illnesses, a low fee will be charged. The doctor will first indicate the surgery price list set by the society and carry out the surgery after obtaining the patient's consent and payment. Article 14: In the event of difficult or dangerous illnesses, if the society's doctor believes that hospitalization is necessary, the patient's family should follow the guidance. Article 15: If a member requests a house call from the society's doctor, they must register with the society with their membership card during the prescribed hours. The fee for a specialist doctor is eight yuan in national currency, and the fee for a doctor on duty is four yuan in national currency. The fee for emergency visits is doubled. The consultation fee must be paid in full at the time of registration. Telephone registration is invalid. Article 16: According to the usual practice for doctors' house calls, a acquaintance's introduction is required, and the consent of the doctor making the house call is also needed. Article 17: The society has specially contracted phototherapy specialists and chemical testing specialists to conduct tests. Members may enjoy preferential treatment if they request tests or if tests are necessary for illnesses. Article 18: If ten or more society members need vaccination and epidemic prevention injections, they may consult with the society to arrange for personnel to be sent to their location at no additional charge. Article 19: If members, due to a large number of people or being far away, request that the society's doctor visit their location for consultation, the method should be negotiated with the society by the person in charge of the group. Article 20: The society has separate maternity insurance measures, and members can enjoy preferential treatment. Article 21: The society will plan to hold various health campaigns from time to time, such as group check-ups, group trips, health lectures, etc., and members may participate at will and enjoy excellent treatment. Article 22: Members may read the society's publications on instilling health knowledge for free or at a low price. Article 23: Members who purchase life insurance from the society may enjoy preferential insurance rates. Article 24: Members who have not visited the society for outpatient treatment or invited the society's doctor for a house call within one year will have their membership fee for the next year calculated at 20% off to show preferential treatment. Article 25: If a member withdraws from the society or leaves the city midway, the membership fee will not be refunded. Article 26: If a member's address changes, they must notify the society in writing for record-keeping. Article 27: If a membership card is lost, it must be guaranteed by two or more people and a handling fee must be paid: three corners of national currency for basic members and one yuan for special members before a replacement can be issued. Article 28: Membership cards may not be transferred or lent to others. Article 29: These rules may be amended at any time if there are any matters not covered.

Maternity Insurance Measures

At the same time, maternity insurance measures have also been formulated for pregnant women to ensure the safety of childbirth. The original text states: (1) The society has special maternity reservation certificates, which are divided into the following three types: Type A maternity reservation certificate, 60 yuan in national currency; Type B maternity reservation certificate, 28 yuan in national currency; Type C maternity reservation certificate, 10 yuan in national currency. If a society member reserves maternity care, Type A will be reduced by 10 yuan and calculated as 50 yuan, and Type B will be reduced by 3 yuan and calculated as 25 yuan to show preferential treatment. However, Type C does not differentiate between members and non-members. (2) Type A and Type B maternity insurance must be purchased no later than the eighth month of pregnancy. (3) Type A maternity insurance enjoys the following benefits: 1. From the date of purchase of the insurance until delivery, you can come to the society for free examination and treatment at any time with the certificate. However, inviting the society's doctor for a house call must be handled in accordance with Article 15 of the society's member treatment guidelines. If a member requests a house call from the society's doctor, they must register with the society with their membership card during the prescribed hours. The fee for a specialist doctor is eight yuan in national currency, and the fee for a doctor on duty is four yuan in national currency. The fee for emergency visits is doubled. The consultation fee must be paid in full at the time of registration. Telephone registration is invalid. 2. During delivery, you can stay in the first-class ward of the hospital designated by the society. (If the first-class ward is full, you can stay in the second-class ward without additional charges.) 3. Regardless of whether it is a normal or difficult delivery, the surgery fee and the materials, medicines, and baby food used during hospitalization are not charged separately. 4. Outpatient or house call visits for the mother and baby within six days after discharge are free of charge. However, the free hospitalization time is determined by the society's doctor. If you voluntarily extend your hospitalization time, all expenses during this period must be borne by yourself. (4) Type B maternity insurance allows you to stay in the third-class ward of the hospital designated by the society, and the rest is handled according to the Type A method. (5) Type C maternity insurance only covers normal delivery and does not provide hospitalization. The society will send a doctor to the pregnant woman's home to deliver the baby. All prenatal outpatient examinations, outpatient and house call visits within six days after delivery, and materials and medicines used during delivery are included and will not be charged separately. In the event of a difficult delivery, the surgery fee and hospitalization fee must be borne by yourself. (6) For Type A and Type B, if you voluntarily deliver at home, you must obtain the permission of the society's doctor, but the hospitalization fee will not be refunded. In the event of a difficult delivery, you must still be sent to the hospital, otherwise it will be considered a termination of the insurance midway. (7) After purchasing maternity insurance, miscarriage or premature birth will be counted as normal birth. (8) Pregnant women who purchase maternity insurance must first be examined by the society's doctor. In special circumstances, the society may not accept the insurance purchase. (9) Diseases unrelated to childbirth will not be accepted. If you are a society member, you can enjoy the rights of a society member separately. (10) The delivery doctor will be selected and sent by the society and cannot be designated. (11) Those who purchase maternity insurance must fill in their name, age, place of origin, address, and guarantor on the certificate, and it is only allowed to be used by the person who purchased the insurance and will be invalid after delivery and cannot be transferred or lent to others. (12) These measures may be amended at any time if there are any matters not covered.
